Topic 5: Characteristics of the Applications 107 
 Topic 5: Characteristics of the Applications 
 
   In order to cultivate the applications, one must first understand them. For this purpose, the characteristics of the applications are presented as the fifth topic. A characteristic of an application refers to a yoga of the path perfection of wisdom. The path perfection of wisdom is a case of giving the name of the result, the perfection of wisdom, to the cause, the path that leads to the attainment of the resultant perfection of wisdom. Therefore, a yoga of the path perfection of wisdom is describing a practice of such a path perfection of wisdom. The different types of characteristics are yogas of a path perfection of wisdom and are taught to enhance an understanding of the bodhisattvas application.   The word characteristic is used throughout this topic to translate the Tibetan 
word, mtshan nyid  (pronounced tsen nyi ). However, in general, mtshan nyid  is 
translated as definition. A specific phenomenon will have only one specific definition. One should keep in mind these different possible meanings of mtshan 
nyid when going through this topic, for in some cases although characteristic is 
used, the meaning may come closer to that of definition. 
 
The definition of a yoga of the path perfection of wisdom is  a bodhisattvas yoga conjoined 
with a union of calm abiding and special insight that is the means for attaining a 
resultant perfection of wisdom that is its object of attainment.68  
 
Boundaries : It exists from the Mahayana path of accumulation through the end of the 
continuum as a sentient being. 
 
4.13 That which characterizes, by means of that, is to be understood  
As being the characteristics. Moreover, there are three types: 
The knowledge, differentiating and functional. The entities are also what are characterized.  
 
  
Topic 5: Characteristics of the Applications 108 
 There are four types of characteristics, namely: 
1. knowledge characteristics ( shes mtshan ) 
2. differentiating characteristics ( khyad mtshan )  
3. functional characteristics ( byed mtshan ) 
4. entity characteristics ( ngo bo nyid mtshan ) 
 
 The first three types of characteristics act to characterize any of the general and specific applications of the three exalted knowers; hence, the term characteristic is applied to them. The fourth type, entity characteristics, are the bases on which these other characteristics are applied, since the entity characteristics are illustrations of the applications. However, it is suitable to call this fourth type characteristic because it also enable us to understand the applications.   These are applied in relation to three things: 
1. That which is characterized . This is what we want to understand. 
2. Characteristic . This helps us to understand that which is characterized. 
3. Illustration.
69 This is the basis upon which one applies an understanding of 
the characteristics and that which is characterized.  
  To assist in understanding this, we can make use of the example of fire: 
a. Fire itself as that which is characterized, i.e., what we want to understand. 
b. Its characteristics are hot and burning. This helps us to understand what 
fire is. 
c. We can use the fire from burning grass as an illustration.  
 
Having observed that the fire from burning grass is hot and burning, we come to know fire, which is characterized by being hot and burning.  The knowledge characteristics characterize the applications of each of the three exalted knowers  knower of bases, knower of paths, and exalted knower of all aspects  in relation to what is known by them. There are sixteen characteristics for each of the three exalted knowers, making a total of forty-eight knowledge characteristics.  There are sixteen differentiating characteristics that characterize the applications as superior to the applications of hearers and solitary realizers, while the eleven functional characteristics characterize the applications as having the special function of bringing about the welfare of sentient beings. The sixteen entity characteristics are 
Topic 5: Characteristics of the Applications 109 
 the actual applications themselves, and they are the illustrations upon which we will 
build up our understanding of the applications.  By studying these four types of characteristics, we will come to understand: 
• what knowledge is gained through the applications, 
• in what way are the bodhisattvas applications superior to those of hearers and 
solitary realizers, 
• how the applications bring about the welfare of sentient beings, and 
• the actual applications themselves. 
1. Knowledge Characteristics 
The knowledge characteristics of the applications in the three exalted knowers can 
be summarized in the following way:  
For the knower of bases: 
!  That which is characterized  is an application in the knower of bases in the 
continuum of a bodhisattva. 
!  The characteristic  is a bodhisattvas yoga abiding in a class of Hinayana 
realization70 that observes any of the aspects of a knower of bases, such as 
knowing the arising of a tathagata (the knowledge characteristics of a knower of bases). 
!  An illustration  is the bodhisattvas yoga that is devoid of afflictions, signs and so 
forth (the first four of the sixteen entity characteristics). 
 
For the knower of paths: 
!  That which is characterized  is an application in the knower of paths. 
!  The characteristic  is a bodhisattvas yoga that observes any of the aspects of a 
knower of paths, such as empty and signless (the knowledge characteristics of a knower of paths). 
!  An illustration  is the bodhisattvas yoga of achieving, such as the difficult wearing 
of the armor of others welfare (the next five entity characteristics). 
 
For the exalted knower of all aspects: 
! That which is characterized  is an application in the exalted knower of all aspects. 
! The characteristic  is a bodhisattvas yoga that observes any of the aspects of an 
exalted knower of all aspects, such as abiding in the happiness of the present 
Topic 5: Characteristics of the Applications 110 
 life due to Tathagatas dharma (the knowledge characteristics of an exalted 
knower of all aspects). 
! An illustration  is the bodhisattvas yoga that observes any of the aspects of an 
exalted knower of all aspects, such as the features of bases and paths (the last seven entity characteristics). 
 The detailed presentation of the knowledge characteristics is in three sections: 
a. Knowledge characteristics of the application in a knower of bases 
b. Knowledge characteristics of the application in a knower of paths c. Knowledge characteristics of the application in an exalted knower of all 
aspects 
a. Knowledge characteristics of the application in a knower of bases 
The definition of a knowledge characteristic of an application in a knower of bases in a 
bodhisattvas continuum is  a bodhisattvas yoga abiding in a type of Hinayana 
realization that observes any of the aspects of a knower of bases such as the arisal of a 
tathagata .71

2. Differentiating Characteristics 
The definition of an application superior to a hearers and solitary realizers application is  a 
bodhisattvas yoga qualified by inconceivability and so forth.74  
 
4.23 The object-possessors ranging over the truths are differentiated 
By means of the attributes of inconceivable and so forth: 
These are explained as the differentiating characteristics By way of the sixteen moments.   
 
Topic 5: Characteristics of the Applications 115 
 The sixteen moments of the Mahayana path of seeing are differentiated from the 
applications of hearers and solitary realizers by the differentiating characteristics of inconceivable, unequaled and so forth. These sixteen moments  the Dharma forbearances, Dharma knowledges, subsequent forbearances, and subsequent knowledges  have the four noble truths as their observed objects and are subjects (object-possessors) that realize the reality of true suffering as inconceivable and so forth.  Although this explanation is given in relation to the sixteen moments of the path of seeing by taking them as the basis of differentiation from the applications of hearers and solitary realizers, these sixteen differentiating characteristics already exist from the path of accumulation upward. 
 
4.24 Inconceivable, unequaled, 
Perfectly transcending comprehension, and counting, 
A composite of all superiors, that which is cognized By the wise, knowing the unshared,   
4.25 Knowing quickly, not decreasing or increasing, 
Accomplishing, perfectly accomplishing, 
Observing, along with support, 
All, cared for,      
4.26 Not relishing: It is superior 
In that it is understood to be the essence of the sixteen. Due to that, this path is a special path Since it is superior to others.   
 
 The applications of the bodhisattva are superior to those of the hearers and solitary realizers by the way of the following sixteen differentiating characteristics, which is to be understood as the essence of the sixteen moments, the object-possessors of the four noble truths.   
Topic 5: Characteristics of the Applications 116 
 The forbearances and knowledges whose observed object is true sufferings: 
1. understand the inconceivable reality of true sufferings. 
2. realize the reality of true sufferings is unequaled because it is without analogy. 3. realize the reality of true sufferings that perfectly transcends comprehension 
by a conventional valid cognizer. 
4. realize the reality of true sufferings that perfectly transcends being counted by 
numbers. 
 
The forbearances and knowledges whose observed object is true origins: 
1. are a condensation of all excellent qualities of all superiors. 
2. know that which is cognized by the wise since they are beings who know the 
modes and varieties. 
3. thoroughly know the vast and profound things that are not shared by hearers 
and solitary realizers. 
4. know quickly ones own Mahayana system. 
 
The forbearances and knowledges whose observed object is true cessations: 
1. realize that all phenomena that depend upon conventional and ultimate 
truths have the entity of not ultimately decreasing or increasing. 
2. accomplish the six perfections by the purities of the three spheres of an 
ultimate object to be given, an ultimate giver and so forth. 
3. perfectly accomplish the collections of merit and wisdom over many eons with 
perfect application that is respectful and continuous. 
4. conjoined with method, observe all phenomena non-conceptually. 
 The forbearances and knowledges whose observed object is true paths: 
1. possess the lineage, the entity of the sphere of reality, the support of the 
bodhisattvas path. 
2. possess the complete collection of causes, the ten perfections, prayer and so 
forth. 
3. are completely under the care of a virtuous spiritual friend who teaches the 
complete path. 
4. do not relish strong adhering to true existence of any phenomena of cyclic 
existence and nirvana. 
 
Topic 5: Characteristics of the Applications 117 
  Having presented the Mahayana applications, the applications of hearers and 
solitary realizers that are differentiated from them are not explicitly explained. However, these should be understood to be without the various differentiating characteristics and together with strong adherence to true existence. 
3. Functional Characteristics 
The definition of an application possessing the special function of bringing about others 
welfare is  a bodhisattvas yoga possessing the special function of benefit, happiness, 
protection, and so forth.75  
 
4.27 Benefiting, happiness and protecting, 
A refuge for human beings, 
Place, helper, island, Known as a leader,     
4.28 Spontaneously accomplishing, not actualizing 
The result of the three vehicles, and The last, the activity of support: These are the functional characteristics. 
 
The applications that are differentiated from those of hearers and solitary realizers also possess the special functions of bringing about others welfare. There are eleven of these functional characteristics, which are divided into three groups:  
! three functional characteristics of the applications in the knower of bases 
! seven functional characteristics of the applications in the knower of paths 
! one functional characteristic of the applications in the exalted knower of all aspects 
 The functional characteristics of applications in the knower of bases are: 
1. Benefit   Bringing about future benefit by setting sentient beings on the path 
to liberation. 
Topic 5: Characteristics of the Applications 118 
 2. Happiness   Providing the happiness of this life, such as pacifying suffering 
and mental unhappiness. 
3. Protection   Protecting from the sufferings of cyclic existence and making them 
not ripen again. 
 
The functional characteristics of applications in the knower of paths are: 
4. A refuge for humans   Placing sentient beings in the lasting benefit of nirvana. 
5. [Resting] place   Setting sentient beings in a state in which the causes of 
suffering have been eliminated. 
6. Helper   Placing sentient beings in the realization of the equality of cyclic 
existence and nirvana. 
7. Island   Supporting the realization of ones own and others welfare by setting 
them in the liberation that is free from the moisture of craving. 
8. Known as a leader   Accomplishing the temporal and ultimate welfare of 
others. 
9. Spontaneous   Spontaneously accomplishing the welfare of sentient beings. 
Spontaneous here means no effort is needed. 
10. The result of the three vehicles is not actualized   Not actualizing the perfect end at 
the wrong time. 
 The functional characteristic of applications in the exalted knower of all aspects is: 
11. The last, the activity of supporting   As a support of the transitory (i.e., the 
world), teaching all phenomena in accordance with others wishes. 
4. Entity Characteristics 
4.29 Afflictive emotions, signs, marks, 
Devoid of the discordant class and  
Antidotes, difficult, definite, Object of intent, not observed,     
4.30 Stopping strong adherence, 
That known as observing, Clashing, without impediment, 
Topic 5: Characteristics of the Applications 119 
 No basis, not progressing, no production, 
 
4.31 Thusness not observed: 
These essences that are the sixteen entities, Since serving to characterize like a definiendum, Are asserted as the fourth characteristic.  
 
The sixteen entity characteristics are illustrations for understanding the applications, like illustrating a definiendum. They are presented in relation to the three exalted knowers.  
In relation to application in the knower of bases: 
1. Afflictions  An application that is an abandonment of afflictions, such as 
attachment. 
2. Signs  An application that is an abandonment of the signs of afflictions, such 
as bad bodily states. 
3. Marks   An application that is an abandonment of improper mental 
attention, the mark that is the cause of afflictions. 
4. Discordant classes and antidotes   An application that is qualified by being 
devoid of the conception of true existence of the two, objects to be discarded and objects to be adopted. 
 
In relation to application in the knower of paths: 
5. Difficult   An application that accomplishes the difficult [task] of placing 
sentient beings, who do not exist ultimately, conventionally in nirvana. 
6. Definite   An application that is definite to accomplish buddhahood 
unequivocally without falling into other vehicles. 
7. Objects of intent   An application that accomplishes the three great objects of 
intent (great heroic mind/compassion, great abandonment, and great realization), which are accomplished over a long period. 
8. Not observed   An application that realizes that the object of meditation and 
the meditator are not observed as ultimate. 
9. Stop strong adherence   An application that stops strong adherence to things as 
truly existent. 
Topic 5: Characteristics of the Applications 120 
  
In relation to application in the exalted knower of all aspects: 
10. Known as observing   An application that observes the distinction of things, the 
bases and paths, which are included in the objects of an exalted knower of all 
aspects and a knower of paths. 
11. Clashes   An application that teaches a path that clashes with the childish 
ones, since it teaches the opposite of adherence to true existence. 
12. Without impediment   An application that knows form and so forth without 
any obstruction. 
13. Baseless   An application that knows there is no basis of error since objects of 
knowledge and knowledge itself are not observed to truly exist. 
14. No progressing   An application that knows there is no going anywhere 
ultimately since suchness is empty of true existence. 
15. No production   An application that knows no production since forms and so 
forth do not exist ultimately. 
16. Not observing thusness   An application that realizes that thusness of the three 
(functioning thing, non-functioning thing, and both) is not observed ultimately. 
Conclusion 
In summary, there are four types of characteristics with a total of ninety-one characteristics that help us develop a deeper understanding of the applications. The forty-eight knowledge characteristics indicate what knowledge is gained by the applications in each of the three exalted knowers. The sixteen differentiating characteristics indicate how these bodhisattva applications are superior to those of hearers and solitary realizers. The eleven functional characteristics indicate the special functions or benefits of the applications. Finally, the sixteen entity characteristics are the actual applications that serve as the bases for illustrating the previous three characteristics.

Topic 6: Mahayana Partial Concordance with Liberation 122 
 Topic 6:  Mahayana Partial Concordance with Liberation 
 
   After explaining the characteristics of the applications, the Mahayana partial concordance with liberation is presented in order to help the trainee understand that the characteristics of the applications are only generated in those bodhisattvas who have entered the Mahayana partial concordance with liberation.   Partial concordance with liberation is synonymous with the path of accumulation. Upon entering the path of accumulation, one enters the first path that leads to liberation. Thus, the path of accumulation is a path that is partially concordant or harmonious with the attainment of liberation and, therefore, is called partial concordance with liberation. In other words, a partial concordance with liberation promotes the attainment of liberation. The Hinayana partial concordance with liberation promotes the attainment of individual liberation, while the Mahayana partial concordance with liberation promotes the attainment of complete enlightenment. This topic pertains to the Mahayana partial concordance with liberation, or the Mahayana path of accumulation.  Upon generating uncontrived bodhichitta, a trainee simultaneously enters the Mahayana path, becomes a bodhisattva, and generates the Mahayana partial concordance with liberation in his continuum. The Mahayana partial concordance with liberation is the first of five paths of the bodhisattva.
76 It marks the start of the 
accumulation of the three countless great eons of merit needed to attain buddhahood. The first countless great eon of merit is accumulated on the Mahayana paths of accumulation and preparation, the second is accumulated from the Mahayana path of seeing through the seventh bodhisattva ground, and the third is accumulated on the three pure grounds, the eighth through the tenth bodhisattva grounds.   
The definition of partial concordance with liberation explicitly indicated in this case is  a clear 
realizer of doctrine of a bodhisattva skilled in achieving an exalted knower of all 
aspects in his own continuum.77  
 
Boundaries : It is only on the Mahayana path of accumulation. 
 
 
Topic 6: Mahayana Partial Concordance with Liberation 123 
 This topic will be described in three sections: 
1. General description of partial concordance with liberation 
2. The measure of skill in the five factors 
3. Identifying the trainees of Ornament  who are skilled in the five factors 
1. General description of partial concordance with liberation 
4.32 Skill in perfectly accomplishing 
The signless, great generosity and so forth, 
In this the realization of all aspects Is asserted as the partial concordance with liberation.   
 
What is a Mahayana  partial concordance with liberation? It is a clear realizer of the 
doctrine in the continuum of a bodhisattva who is skilled in achieving 
enlightenment through the practice of the six perfections  generosity, ethics, patience, joyous effort, concentration, and wisdom  while understanding that they are empty of true existence. In other words, the aim of the Mahayana path of accumulation is enlightenment; to achieve this, the bodhisattva must become skilled in practicing the six perfections while not conceiving them to be truly existent. Here, one gains an experience of emptiness by way of a wisdom arisen from reflecting.
78 
The bodhisattva must continue to practice in this way until the achievement of his goal, buddhahood. 
2. The measure of skill in the five factors 
4.33 Faith observing the buddhas and so forth,  
Joyous effort in the objects of practice, generosity and so forth,  
Mindfulness, the perfect thought,  Non-analytic meditative stabilization, and  
 
4.34ab The wisdom that knows all phenomena  
In all ways: these are the five types.  
 
Topic 6: Mahayana Partial Concordance with Liberation 124 
  What is meant by skill in practicing the six perfections? In this context, skill is 
measured in terms of five factors: 
1. Faith  observing the Three Jewels in general, and the uncommon refuge of the 
Mahayana, the Mahayana paths and its results, in particular. Faith is the root 
of all excellent qualities. One must take all the Mahayana paths and results as an object of ones faith and continuously familiarize oneself with them, whereby one will establish the root of the Mahayana in oneself. Although this 
verse ( Faith observing buddha and so forth)  refers to taking refuge, skill in faith 
is presented first in order to identify it as the root of the Mahayana path. 
2. Joyous effort  ranging over the six perfections. One who delights in practicing 
the six perfections and all Mahayana paths is called skilled in effort. It is 
important for a bodhisattva to exert effort in his practice after developing bodhichitta. If he does not do so, he will not attain enlightenment.  
3. Mindfulness  of the perfect thought. Here, perfect thought refers to 
bodhichitta, which is the doorway to entering the Mahayana path. Bodhichitta, or the mind of enlightenment, is the perfect thought of the Mahayana. One who remains mindful of the goal, enlightenment, for the sake of others has skill with respect to mindfulness.  
4. Non-analytical meditative stabilization  refers to single-pointedly focusing on an 
object using stabilizing meditation. One first observes an image, such as a 
statue of the holy body of a tathagata, without analysis. Then, in dependence 
on the nine stages of calm abiding, one familiarizes with it until one engages that object without effort and without any need to apply the antidotes to laxity and excitement. One continues in this manner until one generates the bliss of physical and mental pliancy. At this time, one has attained calm abiding. There are two types of calm abiding: common calm abiding, which exists even in the continua of non-Buddhists, and uncommon calm abiding, which exists only in the continua of bodhisattvas on the fifth ground and above. 
5. Wisdom  that knows all phenomena in all ways. In dependence on the 
attainment of actual calm abiding, one then gains a special insight knowing all the aspects of objects of knowledge, the phenomena that are modes and varieties, by which one becomes skilled in the five factors. This includes the special insight that understands the way phenomena exist conventionally (varieties) as well as the way they exist ultimately (modes). Special insight also has two types: common special insight, which is also present in the continua 
Topic 6: Mahayana Partial Concordance with Liberation 125 
 of non-Buddhists, and uncommon special insight, which is present only in the 
continua of Buddhists.  
3. Identifying the trainees of Ornament  who are skilled in the five factors 
4.34cd Complete enlightenment is asserted to be  
Easily realized by the sharp, difficult to be realized by the dull.  
 
In general, a trainee who studies Ornament  is of sharp faculty; among these are 
followers of Dharma and followers of faith. A bodhisattva who is a follower of 
Dharma attains complete enlightenment easily in a short period of time, whereas a follower of faith attains it with difficulty over a long period of time. The measure of one being a follower of Dharma or a follower of faith depends on the strength of the five factors described above. If the five factors are strong, one is a follower of Dharma, whereas if they are weak, one is a follower of faith. Followers of Dharma are also quick with regard to their speed of analysis; they follow the teachings only after examining and analyzing the content of what has been taught. In contrast, followers of faith are generally slower in analysis; they follow the teachings only out 
of faith, without analyzing the teachings. In general, a trainee intent on Ornament  is 
a follower of Dharma. 
Conclusion 
In conclusion, in order to attain enlightenment one must first accumulate three 
countless great eons of merit, which begins on the Mahayana partial concordance with liberation, or path of accumulation. This is done by becoming skilled in practicing the six perfections with an understanding that all phenomena are empty of true existence. Skill is measured in terms of five factors: faith, effort, mindfulness, meditative stabilization, and wisdom. 
Topic 7: Mahayana Partial Concordance with Definite Discrimination 126 
 Topic 7:  Mahayana Partial Concordance with Definite 
Discrimination 
 
   This topic discusses the Mahayana partial concordance with definite discrimination, 
o r  t h e  M a h a y a n a  p a t h  o f  p r e p a r a t i o n ,  w h i c h  i s  t h e  s e c o n d  o f  t h e  f i v e  M a h a y a n a  
paths. After completing the first path, the Mahayana path of accumulation, the bodhisattva enters the Mahayana path of preparation upon generating a union of calm abiding and special insight observing emptiness.  The Mahayana partial concordance with definite discrimination has four levels: 
1. heat  
2. peak 3. tolerance  4. supreme mundane qualities 
 
 Within each level, there are two periods: (a) meditative equipoise, when the bodhisattva is meditating on emptiness, and (b) subsequent attainment, which occurs subsequent to meditative equipoise. Subsequent attainment consists of periods when the bodhisattva is not meditating on emptiness, such as times when meditating on other objects such as impermanence, or times when practicing the perfections such as generosity. This topic, the Mahayana partial concordance with 
definite discrimination explicitly indicated in this case , focuses on the subsequent 
attainment period of the Mahayana partial concordance with definite 
discrimination, describing the realizations and practices of this bodhisattva when he is not meditating on emptiness.  
The definition of Mahayana partial concordance with definite discrimination explicitly 
indicated in this case is  a bodhisattvas clear realizer of meaning explicitly indicated in 
this case, qualified mainly by a factor of method.79  
 
Boundaries : It is only on the Mahayana path of preparation.  
Topic 7: Mahayana Partial Concordance with Definite Discrimination 127 
 4.35 Here, the observed objects of the heat levels 
Are commended to be all sentient beings.  
Impartial mind toward them and so forth  Are explained to be the ten types.  
4.36 Oneself turning away from negativities and  
Abiding in generosity and so forth, Thereby setting others in them,  Expressing praise, and conforming:  
4.37 This is the peak. Likewise, tolerance is 
Oneself and those having a different basis knowing the truths. Supreme quality is to be understood similarly since Acting to ripen sentient beings and so forth. 
 
 Here, the observed objects  and aspects  of subsequent attainment of the Mahayana 
path of preparation are explained. The observed object  of bodhisattvas on all levels of 
the Mahayana path of preparation during subsequent attainment is all sentient 
beings. In other words, when not meditating on emptiness, this bodhisattvas mind 
is oriented toward all sentient beings. The aspects  describe the particular attitudes 
and actions regarding sentient beings that a bodhisattva has over the four levels of 
the path of preparation. There are nineteen aspects presented in this context.  Since the observed object of all four levels of the path of preparation is the same, i.e., all sentient beings, only the aspects are described below.  
1. Heat level 
The aspects of the heat level are the ten types of mind toward sentient beings. These are the ten types of mind that a bodhisattva generates on the heat level of the path of preparation.  
Topic 7: Mahayana Partial Concordance with Definite Discrimination 128 
 Small Heat 
1.  Evenmindedness/equanimity   The bodhisattva regards all sentient beings 
equanimously, ceasing attachment and aversion to them. 
2.  A mind of love   The bodhisattva regards all sentient beings with a mind of 
love as well as with a mind of compassion. These two attitudes accompany 
each other, one being manifest when the other not. Love wishes all sentient beings to have happiness and its causes, while compassion wishes them to be free from suffering and its causes. 
Middling Heat 
3.  A mind of benefit   A bodhisattva thinks how to benefit, help, and serve 
sentient beings. He tries to think of all the possible ways and means to benefit sentient beings and not harm them. There are many ways to harm sentient beings; one should avoid harming them physically, verbally, and mentally. 
4.  A mind of non-anger   This bodhisattva does not become angry with other 
sentient beings. It is good if we also strive not to become angry. When anger arises in us, it creates unhappiness for both ourselves and other sentient beings. 
5.  A mind of non-harmfulness   The bodhisattva is not mean, directly or indirectly. 
We should practice likewise. It is very easy for us to be harmful. Sometimes people do not harm others directly, but indirectly they inflict great harm. 
Great Heat 
6.  The mind of a mother and father   The bodhisattva regards and treats sentient 
beings who are of similar age to his parents as his father and mother. We 
should also practice in this way.  
7.  The mind of a brother and sister   The bodhisattva regards and treats sentient 
beings who are a bit older or younger in age to himself as his brother or sister. 
8.  The mind of a son and daughter   The bodhisattva regards and treats sentient 
beings who are the age of his own children as his own son or daughter. 
9.  The mind of a friend and companion   The bodhisattva regards and treats 
sentient beings who are equal in age to himself as his friends and 
companions. Companions are those with whom one shares ones life, ones girlfriend or boyfriend, and so forth. 
10. The mind of a paternal relative and maternal relative   The bodhisattva regards 
and treats sentient beings as paternal and maternal relatives, grandfather, grandmother, and so forth. 
Topic 7: Mahayana Partial Concordance with Definite Discrimination 129 
 2. Peak level 
Bodhisattvas who abide on the peak level of the path of preparation also have all 
sentient beings as their observed object. There are three aspects or perfect thoughts on the peak level: 
1. The mind of placing others in positive activities: 
• Small peak   The mind of turning away from the ten non-virtues and 
placing others likewise. 
• Middling peak   The mind of abiding in generosity and so forth and 
similarly placing others in these activities. 
• Great peak   Meditating on the emptiness of the internal and exhorting 
others to meditate on it. 
2. Verbally expressing praise for those who engage in these without being 
exhorted to do so. 
3. The mind of rejoicing in those who act in accordance with the previous two 
aspects. 
3. Tolerance level 
The tolerance level also observes all sentient beings by way of three aspects: 
1. The mind of placing others in positive activities: 
• Small tolerance   Abiding in the knowledge of the four noble truths and 
placing others in this knowledge and so forth. 
• Middling tolerance   Abiding in the knowledge that although one 
understands the results of stream enterer80 and so forth, one does not 
actualize them. One also places others in this knowledge. 
• Great tolerance   Abiding in the cause of the path of seeing of a bodhisattva 
and placing others in this cause. 
2. Verbally expressing praise for those who engage in these without being 
exhorted to do so. 
3. The mind of rejoicing in those who act in accordance with the previous two 
aspects. 
Topic 7: Mahayana Partial Concordance with Definite Discrimination 130 
 4. Supreme mundane qualities level 
Likewise, the bodhisattva on the supreme mundane qualities level observes all 
sentient beings by way of three aspects. It observes sentient beings by way of ripening them, liberating them, and so forth.  
1. The mind of placing others in positive activities: 
• Small supreme mundane qualities   Abiding in the activity of ripening 
sentient beings and placing others in this activity. 
• Middling supreme mundane qualities   Abiding in the generation of 
clairvoyances and placing others in this activity. 
• Great supreme mundane qualities   Abiding in the activity of generating a 
knower of all aspects and abandoning the afflictions that are induced by latencies and so forth, and placing others in these activities.  
2. Verbally expressing praise for those who engage in these without being 
exhorted to do so. 
3. The mind of rejoicing in those who act in accordance with the previous two 
aspects. 
Conclusion 
In short, during the subsequent attainment period of the Mahayana partial concordance with definite discrimination, the second of the five Mahayana paths, 
the bodhisattva mainly focuses on the practice of method. The observed object  of the 
bodhisattvas during this period is all sentient beings. The bodhisattva observes these sentient beings by means of nineteen aspects , or perfect thoughts and actions: ten 
aspects on the heat level, three aspects on the peak level, three aspects on the 
tolerance level, and three aspects on the supreme mundane qualities level. On the heat level, the bodhisattva generates ten types of virtuous minds toward sentient beings. On each of the peak, tolerance, and supreme mundane qualities levels, the bodhisattva generates three types of mind  (1) the mind of placing others in positive activities, (2) the mind of expressing praise for those who engage similarly without exhortation, and (3) the mind of rejoicing in those who act accordingly. Likewise, we should all try to practice in these ways.  
Topic 8: Signs of Irreversibility  131 
 Topic 8:  Signs of Irreversibility 
 
   On the Mahayana partial concordance with definite discrimination (Mahayana path of preparation) described above, a special group of bodhisattvas is found. These are the irreversible bodhisattva sangha who possess the signs of irreversibility. They are irreversible from highest complete enlightenment and are definite to attain the enlightenment of the buddhas because they will never give up their bodhichitta motivation and regress to a lower vehicle. These bodhisattvas display special signs, known as the signs of irreversibility, whereby others can infer their attainment of irreversibility.  However, one who will definitely attain highest complete enlightenment is not necessarily a bodhisattva who possesses the signs of irreversibility. From the great level of the Mahayana path of accumulation onward, a bodhisattva who is of indefinite lineage will not fall to a lesser vehicle path. It is not possible for him to degenerate from the Mahayana mind of enlightenment, and he will definitely attain highest complete enlightenment. But he is not posited as a bodhisattva who possesses the signs of irreversibility. Likewise, there exists a person who has awakened his Mahayana lineage prior to cultivating the applications, but he too is not posited as among those who possess the signs of irreversibility.  Irreversibility can be understood from two perspectives: 
! From the point of view of thought, one has eliminated the opportunity for 
the arising of the manifest thought of striving for liberation, which is for 
ones welfare alone. 
! From the point of view of training [or conduct], one possesses a stable realization of special method and wisdom. 
  The attainment of irreversibility can be inferred through observing certain signs, such as the following: 
a) The attainment of special wisdom can be inferred by the special verbal sign 
of presenting complete categories of Mahayana paths, such as emptiness. 
b) The special Mahayana method can be inferred by the physical signs of the 
body hair standing on end and tears coming to the eyes, showing that one is unable to bear the suffering of sentient beings. 
Topic 8: Signs of Irreversibility  132 
  
 Furthermore, it can be inferred that someone is irreversible from highest complete enlightenment from the reason that he possesses the powerful causes for enlightenment. How? By the signs of possessing the special method and wisdom mentioned above and by the fact that he has eliminated the occasion of manifesting the thought of striving for his own welfare alone. 
 
The definition of a bodhisattva sangha who has attained the signs of irreversibility is  a 
bodhisattva who has attained in his continuum any of the forty-four signs such as 
having turned away from manifest adhering to the true existence of forms and so 
forth.81  
 
Boundaries : It exists from the heat level of the Mahayana path of preparation through 
the end of the continuum as a sentient being. 
 
Divisions of irreversible bodhisattvas 
4.38 Those bodhisattvas abiding 
From the branches of definite discrimination  
Through the paths of seeing and meditation Are here the assemblies of the irreversible.   
The definition of a sign of irreversibility is  a perfect proof that serves to convince that the 
person who possesses it is irreversible from highest, complete enlightenment.82  
 
 A bodhisattva who has attained any of the forty-four signs of irreversibility is known as a bodhisattva who has attained the signs of irreversibility. There are three divisions of bodhisattva sangha who have attained the signs of irreversibility: 
1. Bodhisattvas of sharp faculties who manifest the signs of irreversibility on the 
Mahayana path of preparation. 
2. Bodhisattvas of middling faculties who manifest the signs of irreversibility on 
the Mahayana path of seeing. 
3. Bodhisattvas of dull faculties who manifest the signs of irreversibility on the 
Mahayana path of meditation. 
Topic 8: Signs of Irreversibility  133 
 These forty-four signs of irreversibility are described in three groups: 
1. signs of irreversibility of one on the path of preparation 
2. signs of irreversibility of one on the path of seeing 3. signs of irreversibility of one on the path of meditation

perfect proof that serves to convince that the bodhisattva on the path of preparation 
who possesses it is irreversible (from highest complete enlightenment).83

There are twenty signs of being irreversible from highest complete enlightenment for 
a sharp-facultied bodhisattva on the path of preparation. These are further divided into the following groups:  
! eleven for the heat level  
! six for the peak level

   The eleven signs on the heat level of path of preparation are: 
1. Turning away from grasping at true existence of phenomena such as forms 
due to realizing their non-true existence. 
2. Extinguishing doubt through attaining faith in the Three Jewels, the 
perfect source of refuge, from having understood them by way of a wisdom arisen from meditation realizing emptiness. 
Topic 8: Signs of Irreversibility  135 
 3. Having prayers for whatever rebirth a bodhisattva desired fulfilled, one 
extinguishes the eight states of non-leisure, namely, birth with wrong 
views, in hells, as a hungry ghost, as an animal, and birth where Buddhas speech cannot be heard, in a barbaric country, with incomplete faculties, such as being stupid or mute, and as a long-life god of Without Discrimination. 
4. Involving oneself and others in virtuous practices through compassion. 
Out of compassion the bodhisattva avoids the ten non-virtues and practices the ten virtues whereby he causes others to engage in these practices. 
5. Generosity and so forth are thoroughly dedicated for the sake of other 
sentient beings due to the bodhisattvas practice of exchanging self and others. 
6. Without a qualm regarding even the meaning of the profound, i.e. 
emptiness, through completely realizing [the reality] of phenomena. 
7. Physical, verbal, and mental actions are motivated by the thought of love 
because the bodhisattva engages in benefiting others without degenerating the thought that wishes all sentient beings to have happiness. 
8. Not being accompanied by the five types of obstructions: (a) desirous 
aspiration, (b) malice, (c) sleep and lethargy, (d) excitement and regret, and (e) doubt, through attaining the perfect training which only exerts effort for others welfare. Sleep and lethargy are counted as one because (i) they 
have the same antidote, (ii) they have the same cause, such as eating food, 
and (iii) they have the same function, being a withdrawing of the mind inside. Food does not refer only to food we eat but also to some events that feed sleep and lethargy: leaning, unhappiness, non-digestion and discouragement. In the case of excitement and regret, the foods that feed them are the different conceptions that arise with respect to ones relatives, friends, companions, and so forth, and with respect to past entertainment, playing, laughing, and enjoyment. These mental factors function to make the mind unruly and the antidote is calm abiding. 
9. Destroying all dormant latencies such as ignorance through thoroughly 
cultivating their antidotes by the power arising from meditating on emptiness. 
10. Possessing mindfulness and alertness through continuous equipoise 
without being distracted to wrong objects at any time. 
Topic 8: Signs of Irreversibility  136 
 11. Dwelling, bedding, clothes, and so forth are clean due to his consistent 
pure behavior. 
  
The six signs on the peak level of the path of preparation are: 
12. The 80,000 types of worms [micro-organisms] do not occur in the body 
through clear superiority over mundane roots of virtue.  
13. Not having a dishonest mind, i.e., not having a deceitful mind that is 
motivated by dissimulation and deceit due to having thoroughly purifying the roots of virtue. 
14. Correctly undertaking the twelve excellent qualities of training of wearing 
clothes from the rubbish and so forth because the bodhisattva has disregard for gain, honor, and so forth. These are a list of trainings, or ascetic practices allowed by the buddha for those who wanted to train in a more ascetic manner to help decrease attachment to food, clothes, dwelling, and so forth. These include wearing robes made from clothes abandoned in cemeteries, eating only from an alms bowl, and so forth. 
15. Not having miserliness, faulty morality, and such contrary qualities due to 
the special practices of the six perfections, generosity, and so forth. 
16. Progressing toward possessing the yoga of the perfection of wisdom, which 
does not contradict reality due to perfectly gathering all phenomena into the emptiness of true existence. 
17. Desiring to take rebirth in hell for the welfare of other sentient beings 
because the bodhisattva considers all migrators as his own child. 
 The two signs on the tolerance level of the path of preparation are: 
18. Not being misled by others who teach other paths due to his confidence in 
the realization of the meaning of reality. 
19. Realizing a mara who is teaching a counterfeit path, such as fasting or 
relying on the five fires, as a mara through skill in knowing the methods to attain buddhahood. 
 The one sign on the supreme mundane qualities level of the path of preparation is: 
20. Pleasing the buddha in all his activities due to the bodhisattvas practice of 
the six perfections by means of the purity of the three spheres.  
Topic 8: Signs of Irreversibility  137 
 2. Signs of Irreversibility of one on the path of seeing 
 
The definition of a sign of irreversibility of a bodhisattva on the path of seeing is  a perfect 
proof that serves to convince that the middling-facultied bodhisattva on the path of 
seeing who possesses it is irreversible from highest complete enlightenment.84  
 
4.46 The sixteen moments of the forbearances and  
Knowledges of the path of seeing, 
Are to be known as the characteristics  of the irreversible bodhisattvas.   
 The special method and wisdom included in the sixteen moments of the path of 
seeing
85 in the continuum of a middling-facultied bodhisattva, along with the special 
physical and verbal signs induced by them, are the signs of irreversibility on the path of seeing.  What are the aspects of these sixteen moments that are the signs of irreversibility?   These sixteen aspects are divided into four groups of four in relation to the four noble truths.  
4.47 Having removed the discrimination of forms and so forth, 
Stable mind, completely turned away from 
Lesser vehicles, thoroughly extinguishing the limbs Of the concentrations and so forth,  
4.48 Lightness of body and mind, 
While enjoying the desirable, being skilled in means, Constantly chaste conduct, Completely pure necessities for livelihood,    
4.49 The aggregates and so forth, those that interfere, 
The collections, the battle of the sense powers 
Topic 8: Signs of Irreversibility  138 
 And so forth, having individually stopped the abiding 
Which is an application and a subsequent application   
4.50 In miserliness and so forth, 
Not observing a mere atom of phenomena, Abiding on the three grounds Certain of ones own ground, and    
4.51 Forsaking life for the sake of the Dharma: 
The sixteen moments which are thus Are the signs of irreversibility Of the wise abiding on the path of seeing.  
The four aspects related to true suffering are: 
1. Removing the seeds of the acquired conception that discriminates forms and 
so forth as truly existent phenomena by means of the direct realization of 
emptiness of their own nature ultimately. 
2. Stable conventional and ultimate mind generations due to the blessings of the 
buddhas and so forth so that the bodhisattva does not degenerate these minds. 
3. Completely turning ones mind away from the lesser vehicles of hearers and 
solitary realizers because, through practicing the special qualities of the Mahayana, there is no occasion of generating the thought seeking liberation for oneself alone. 
4. Thoroughly extinguishing the limbs  that is, the potential  for taking birth 
in the realms of the concentrations and formless absorptions by means of fine discrimination of the reality of phenomena. These potentials for rebirth are due to the power of actions of having attained the concentrations and formless absorptions. 
Topic 8: Signs of Irreversibility  139 
 The four aspects related to true origin are: 
5. Lightness of body and mind, which is the bliss of pliancy, due to being 
separated from non-virtue. 
6. Enjoying the desirables without strong clinging while dwelling among 
householders through being skilled in the means of subduing sentient beings. 
7. Constantly chaste conduct through seeing the shortcomings of desirable sense 
objects. 
8. Completely pure necessities for livelihood through abandoning wrong 
livelihood. 
 
The four aspects related to true cessation are: 
9. Having individually stopped, by means of directly realizing emptiness, (i) 
abiding in the application that initially adheres to the aggregates, constituents, and spheres as truly existent, and (ii) abiding in the subsequent application that subsequently adheres to their true existence, i.e., the continuation of that adherence to true existence. 
10. As before, having stopped adherence to those phenomena that interfere with 
the realization of the Dharma knowledge of true cessation as truly existent through eliminating the objects of abandonment of the Dharma forbearance of true cessation. 
11. As before, having stopped adherence to the collections of enlightenment, 
generosity and so forth, as truly existent through knowing the faults of the conception of true existence.  
12. As before, having individually stopped (i) abiding in the application that 
initially adheres to the true existence of the battle between the objects to be abandoned and the antidote that abandon them, the realization that they do not truly exist, and (ii) abiding in a subsequent application that subsequently adheres to their true existence. The objects to be abandoned are adherence to the true existence of the objects and object-possessors  the sense powers (eye and so forth), indicated in the sutra by the term village, the sense bases, indicated by the term city, the objects of the senses, indicated by the term town, and the beings, indicated by the term consciousness, and so forth. 
Topic 8: Signs of Irreversibility  140 
 The four aspects related to true path are: 
13. Having individually stopped (i) abiding in an application that initially adheres 
to the true existence of the objects of abandonment, miserliness, faulty 
morality and so forth, and (ii) abiding in a subsequent application that afterward adheres to their true existence. This stopping is through attaining and realizing special generosity and so forth. 
14. The phenomena that are realized, the paths and the result  enlightenment  
are not observed to possess even a mere atom of true existence due to the realization of the non-true existence of all phenomena included in entity, cause, and result, which is the nature of the three doors of complete liberation. 
15. Abiding in the certainty that is free from doubt regarding the three grounds 
that are ones personal attainment, which are in the nature of the three exalted knowers of all, through gaining strong confidence in the realization of non-true existence. 
16. Not experiencing even the slightest miserliness or suffering with respect to 
forsaking ones life for the sake of the Dharma, the exalted knower of all aspects and so forth, due to directly realizing the mode of abidance of phenomena and exerting consistent effort toward the final exalted knower of all aspects. 
  On this occasion, the signs of irreversibility, which are the special signs of body 
and speech, are known as the sixteen moments of the path of seeing, even though 
they do not occur during the meditative equipoise of the path of seeing. The purpose of calling them such is to show that the signs arise due to the sixteen moments of the meditative equipoise of the path of seeing. This is a case of giving the name of the cause to the result. 
3. Signs of Irreversibility of one on the path of meditation 
The signs of irreversibility of a dull-facultied bodhisattva on the path of meditation will be explained after having presented the path of meditation: 
  a. Features of the path of meditation   b. Basis of the features, the path of meditation  c. Divisions of the path of meditation  d. Signs of irreversibility on the path of meditation 
Topic 8: Signs of Irreversibility  141 
 a. Features of the path of meditation 
4.52 The path of meditation is profound, 
Since it is profound emptiness and so forth. 
It is profound in that it is free from the extremes  Of superimposition and deprecation.   
The path of meditation has a profound mode of abiding because its mode of abiding 
is thusness, which is qualified by profound emptiness and so forth. That mode of 
abiding is profound because it is a sphere of reality (Skt. dharmadhatu ) that is free 
from the extremes of superimposition and deprecation. In another way, the 
Mahayana path of meditation is profound because of possessing the direct realization of the profound, i.e., thusness. When thusness is profound, the exalted wisdom directly realizing it is also very profound.  When it said profound emptiness and so forth, this refers to the following eleven qualifications: (1) emptiness, (2) signlessness, (3) wishlessness, (4) effortless, (5) non-production, (6) non-cessation, (7) freedom from attachment, (8) cessation, (9) pacification, (10) thusness, and (11) limit of reality.  Superimposition means to impose existence upon that which is non-existent: for example, holding that all phenomena truly exist when, in fact, they are empty of true existence. Deprecation, on the other hand, is to impose non-existence upon that which is existent: for example, holding that if phenomena do not truly exist, then they do not exist at all when, in fact, they do exist. 
b. Basis of the features, the path of meditation 
The definition of a Mahayana path of meditation indicated in this case is  a Mahayana 
subsequent clear realizer arising as an unbroken continuation of what has already 
been realized in the context of the three (paths) of preparation, seeing, and 
meditation which, on the occasion of the branch of definite discrimination, 
repeatedly reflects on the meaning of what has been heard by means of four analytic 
reasonings, on the occasion of the path of seeing, repeatedly assesses the reflected 
meaning by way of the nine (mental states) of calm abiding while set in equipoise, 
and, on the occasion of the path of meditation, repeatedly investigates with certainty 
those nine meanings by means of four special insights that consider, fully 
discriminate, thoroughly investigate, and thoroughly analyze.86  
 
Topic 8: Signs of Irreversibility  142 
 4.53 The path of meditation is that which 
Repeatedly reflects, understands, and definitely investigates 
That on the branches of definite discrimination,  The path of seeing, and the path of meditation itself.  
 
 The path of meditation familiarizes with the realization of emptiness of true existence attained on the paths of preparation, seeing, and meditation. Repeated reflection, which is to analyze the teachings with reasonings after having heard or studied them, occurs on the path of preparation. This refers to the wisdom arisen from hearing and thinking. To understand the meaning is to place the mind single-pointedly on the meaning that was reflected on previously with a mind of calm abiding, which occurs on the path of seeing. To definitely investigate means to investigate the meaning through special insight, by the wisdom arisen from meditation. This takes place on the path of meditation itself. 
c. Divisions of the path of meditation 
4.54 Because it is that which is the continuity, 
It is asserted to be nine-fold 
Due to the aspects of small, middling and great, Being divided into the small of the small and so forth.  
 The Mahayana path of meditation has three principal divisions of small, 
middling, and great levels; each are further subdivided into small, middling, and great. These nine divisions of the path of meditation act as antidotes to the objects of abandonment  the nine divisions of the conception of true existence, which are the knowledge obstructions.  The nine divisions of the path of meditation are generated from small of the small path of meditation through great of the great. These oppose the nine divisions of the objects of abandonment in the order beginning from great of the great level through small of the small level. This way of positing is explained by the analogy of darkness being dispelled by light. A small illumination dispels a great darkness whereas a strong or great illumination is required to dispel a faint darkness. Alternatively, this can be explained using the analogy of removing stains from a cloth by washing. Initially, less effort is needed for the gross stains while increasingly greater effort is needed to remove the more subtle stains. Likewise, a small antidote 
Topic 8: Signs of Irreversibility  143 
 can remove a gross or great obstruction, while a great antidote is needed to remove a 
subtle or small obstruction.  There are disputes that arise from this presentation of the path of meditation regarding, 
(1) the definite enumeration of the divisions of the path of meditation 
(2) the activity of the path of meditation 
 (1) Dispute on the definite enumeration of the divisions of the path of meditation 
A disputant says: It is not correct to assert that the Mahayana path of meditation is 
definitely of only nine divisions because in the three Perfection of Wisdom sutras 
(100,000, 20,000 and 8,000 stanzas) it is said that countless, incomprehensible, and 
immeasurable results and merits are produced in regard to each of the nine divisions of the path of meditation.   
Response: This is refuted by an answer stated in the root text. 
 
4.55 The teachings such as countless and so forth 
Are not adequate with regard to the ultimate: 
The Subduer asserted them to be similar To the cause of mercy conventionally.   
 The teachings regarding countless and so forth results and merit, though 
incorrect since they are inadequate with respect to the ultimate, are not incorrect conventionally. This is because although they are not correct ultimately, the Subduer asserted those results resembling the causes of the mercy of the buddhas conventionally, indicating just how many there are in the sutras.  In other words, the results arising from the path of meditation are countless. Nevertheless, there is no need for the path of meditation not to have definitely nine divisions. This is because the Subduer has seen that the results of the Mahayana path of meditation do not exist ultimately, and yet conventionally, each of the nine divisions of the path yield countless results and infinite merits, which are results similar to the cause  the realization of the sphere of reality that is in the nature of great compassion observing the unapprehendable.  There is a purpose to presenting the generation of countless results from the Mahayana path of meditation. It is in dependence on such a presentation that trainees generate delight in the result, and this, in turn, acts as a cause for entering 
Topic 8: Signs of Irreversibility  144 
 the Mahayana path of meditation. When sentient beings see that there are many 
results from the Mahayana path of meditation, they will engage in it. 
 (2) Dispute on the activity of the path of meditation 
An objection is raised by a challenger who holds the two truths, conventional and ultimate truths, to be contradictory. He holds that: 
a) If something does not exist ultimately or truly, it does not exist at all, and 
b) If something merely exists conventionally, it is only an imaginery and thus 
is unable to perform a function. 
 
 Hence, if the path of meditation does not exist ultimately and merely exists 
conventionally, it is unable to perform the function of acting to abandon the objects of abandonment and progressing to the attainment of enlightenment.  
4.56 Inexpressible things 
Are not suitable to diminish and increase. 
What are diminished and what are attained By the path called meditation?   
 A proponent of true existence asserts that if the path of meditation were empty of 
true existence, it would not exist at all. Hence, the path of meditation could not function to decrease its objects of abandonment nor increase the strength of its antidotes. What is gained and what is diminished through cultivating such a path? It leads nowhere.  
4.57 Enlightenment, likewise that, 
Bring about desired aims. 
Enlightenment has the characteristic of thusness, Also that is asserted as having the characteristic of that.   
Response:  The uncontaminated exalted wisdom of highest complete enlightenment 
does not exist truly or ultimately. Nevertheless, it still conventionally enacts the 
welfare of sentient beings. Likewise, although the Mahayana path of meditation does not truly exist, still it accomplishes the desired aims such as decreasing the objects of abandonment and increasing the strength of antidotes. Therefore, enlightenment is 
Topic 8: Signs of Irreversibility  145 
 the suitable analogy for the Mahayana path of meditation, the actual meaning, 
because they are similar in enacting the special welfare conventionally. Also, just as enlightenment has the characteristic of thusness, i.e., being empty of true existence, likewise, that path of meditation is also asserted as having the characteristic of that thusness.  
4.58ab Regarding enlightenment, former minds 
Are not feasible, nor are later.   
Another disputant holds that even conventionally, the former and later moments of mind generation are unable to produce enlightenment. The reasons are as follows: 
a) Former or latter moments of mind generation does not produce 
enlightenment because all the causes for enlightenment do not appear to each of them. 
b) Former and latter moments of mind generation do not produce 
enlightenment simultaneously because it is impossible for all of them to arise simultaneously. 
c) Former and latter moments of mind generation do not produce 
enlightenment sequentially because as soon as the latter arises, the former has ceased. 
 The mind generation mentioned refers to the two types of mind generations.
87 
  
Response:  If such gradual former and latter moments of mind generation are not truly 
existent, there is not the fault of the absurd consequence of the two combined not 
producing their own result, enlightenment. This is because though not truly existent, through their mutual reliance, the former and latter moments arise consecutively producing their result, highest complete enlightenment.  This can be explained using the analogy of the butter lamp,  
4.58c By means of the analogy of a butter lamp  
  This is like the mutual reliance of the former and latter moments of a butter lamp acting to burn the wick along with the oil. The first moment of the butter lamp alone, without relying on the second moment of the lamp, does not have the ability to completely burn the wick along with the oil. This is because in the first moment there is the simultaneous contact of the flame and the wick. Without a second 
Topic 8: Signs of Irreversibility  146 
 moment, that which burns and that which is burned do not exist because cause and 
effect do not exist simultaneously.  The second moment of the butter lamp alone, without relying on the first moment, does not have the ability to completely burn the wick along with the oil. This is because a second moment cannot arise without relying on the first moment of the butter lamp. If this were not the case, then such a second moment would have to be either a permanent phenomenon (since the second moment can exist independent of a first moment of butter lamp) or non-existent.  Therefore, it is through the mutual reliance of the sequentially arisen former and latter moments of the lamp that the wick and oil are finally consumed. Similarly, through the mutual reliance of the sequentially arisen many former and latter moments of Mahayana mind generation, the result of enlightenment is eventually attained.  In dependence on this explanation using the analogy of a butter lamp, one can also easily realize the eight types of profundities that will be explained. 
d. Signs of irreversibility on the path of meditation 
4.58d Profound reality has eight aspects. 
  Having explained the path of meditation itself, the signs of irreversibility of a bodhisattva on the path of meditation are explained in relation to eight types of profundities. It is through realizing these eight profundities during meditative equipoise that the special verbal and physical signs, the signs of irreversibility, arise during the subsequent attainment.  
4.59 There is profound production, cessation, 
Thusness, objects of knowledge, 
Knowledge, activity,  Non-duality, and skill in means.    
The definition of a sign of irreversibility of a bodhisattva on the path of meditation is  a 
perfect proof that serves to convince that the bodhisattva on the path of meditation 
who possesses it is irreversible from highest complete enlightenment.88  
 
A bodhisattva abiding on the subsequent attainment of the eighth ground understands: 
Topic 8: Signs of Irreversibility  147 
 a. Profound production   Enlightenment is not produced by separate former and 
latter moments of mind generation nor by the simultaneous collection of 
many moments and so forth. Also, enlightenment is not produced independent of such moments. It is through cultivating mind generation that realizations and enlightenment, the object of attainment, are produced. 
b. Profound cessation   All things are ultimately without entity (i.e., true 
existence); therefore, they are ultimately without cessation even though conventionally they cease. 
c. Profound thusness   Although the bodhisattva familiarizes himself with thusness 
by means of wisdom on all occasions of the path, due to compassion he does not actualize thusness (or nirvana) for his own welfare. 
d. Profound objects of knowledge   Although there is no practice of generosity and 
so forth in the nature of thusness of all phenomena, conventionally, a bodhisattva subsequently enacts the practice of the six perfections, such as generosity. 
e. Profound knowledge   All phenomena are of the entity of thusness that is free of 
all elaborations (of true existence); therefore, the non-conceptual exalted wisdom not seeing elaborations is seeing of thusness. 
f. Profound activity   Abiding in reality there is no activity with signs with respect 
to all phenomena, conventionally, there are activities in generosity and so forth. 
g. Profound non-duality  Although ultimately there are not the two, object to be 
achieved and achiever, there is the achieving of all paths through the discrimination with and without signs realizing activity as of the entity of non-duality. 
h. Profound skill in means   Conventionally, there is the completion of the 
collections of merit and wisdom but ultimately their result, the attainment of buddhahood, does not exist. 
  The realization of these eight profundities during the meditative equipoise of the eighth ground induces the special signs of body and speech at subsequent attainment. These are posited as the signs of irreversibility of a bodhisattva on the path of meditation. 
Topic 8: Signs of Irreversibility  148 
 Conclusion 
Therefore, this topic explains the irreversible bodhisattva sangha and the forty-four 
signs of irreversibility. There are twenty signs of irreversibility of bodhisattvas on the Mahayana path of preparation, sixteen on the path of seeing, and eight on the path of meditation. A bodhisattva of sharp faculties attains these signs on the path of preparation, those of middling faculties attain them on the path of seeing, and bodhisattvas of dull faculties will definitely attain the signs on the eighth ground. This is because on the eighth ground, there is no possibility for the thought striving for ones own welfare alone to arise. On lower grounds, it is still possible for such a thought to arise to a slight degree; hence, the lower seven grounds are termed impure grounds, while the eighth through the tenth ground are the pure grounds.
